</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing_campaigns">Marketing campaigns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Marketing campaigns" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>Since its inception, Verizon Communications has run several marketing campaigns, including:
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Can_you_hear_me_now.3F"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Can_you_hear_me_now?">Can you hear me now?</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Can you hear me now?" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The "Can you hear me now?" campaign, which was created for the newly formed Verizon Wireless, started running in 2001 and featured actor <a href="/wiki/Paul_Marcarelli" title="Paul Marcarelli">Paul Marcarelli</a> in the role of "Test Man," a character based on a Verizon network tester who travels the country asking "Can you hear me now?".<sup id="cite_ref-Sentinel00_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sentinel00-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fulford03_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fulford03-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Howard04_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Howard04-141">[141]</a></sup> The campaign, originally conceived by the agency <a href="/wiki/Bozell" title="Bozell">Bozell</a> in New York, ran from early 2001 to September 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Patel11_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Patel11-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Morgranapr11_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morgranapr11-143">[143]</a></sup> Data from the technology tracking firm The <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Group" title="Yankee Group">Yankee Group</a> shows that, in the early years of the campaign, net customers grew 10% to 32.5 million in 2002 and 15% more to 37.5 million in 2003. In addition, customer turnover dropped to 1.8% in 2001, down from 2.5% in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-Howard04_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Howard04-141">[141]</a></sup> In 2011, Marcarelli parted ways with Verizon and is now a spokesperson for <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Corporation" title="Sprint Corporation">Sprint</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="There.27s_a_map_for_that"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="There's_a_map_for_that">There's a map for that</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: There's a map for that" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The "There's a map for that" campaign was launched in late 2009. It was designed as a parody of AT&amp;T's "There's an app for that" adverts. The ads depicted a side-by-side comparison of Verizon and AT&amp;T network coverage maps.<sup id="cite_ref-AP09_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP09-145">[145]</a></sup> AT&amp;T filed a lawsuit in Atlanta federal court early in November 2009, claiming that the coverage maps being used in the ads were misleading.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradley09_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradley09-146">[146]</a></sup> The suit was dropped later that month in conjunction with Verizon dropping a similar suit against AT&amp;T.<sup id="cite_ref-AP09_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP09-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="That.27s_not_cool"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="That's_not_cool">That's not cool</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: That's not cool" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2009, Verizon joined with the <a href="/wiki/Ad_Council" title="Ad Council">Ad Council</a>, in partnership with the <a href="/wiki/Family_Violence_Prevention_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="Family Violence Prevention Fund">Family Violence Prevention Fund</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Office_on_Violence_Against_Women" title="Office on Violence Against Women">Office on Violence Against Women</a>, to create the "That's not cool" campaign. This <a href="/wiki/Public_service_announcement" title="Public service announcement">public service advertising</a> campaign was designed to help teens recognize and prevent digital dating abuse. Verizon ran the ads on its Wireless' Mobile Web service, Verizon FiOS internet and TV.<sup id="cite_ref-MarketingWeekly09_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarketingWeekly09-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shields09_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shields09-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Powerful_Answers">Powerful Answers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Powerful Answers" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In January 2013, Verizon launched the "Powerful Answers" campaign designed by agency <a href="/wiki/McGarryBowen" title="McGarryBowen">McGarryBowen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stibel13_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stibel13-149">[149]</a></sup> The campaign centered around a contest in which $10 million in prizes was offered to individuals for finding solutions to "the world's biggest challenges" by making use of Verizon's cloud, broadband, and wireless networks.<sup id="cite_ref-Wirelessnews14_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wirelessnews14-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mosaritolo13_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mosaritolo13-151">[151]</a></sup> Winners of the inaugural competition were announced at the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">Consumer Electronics Show</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wirelessnews14_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wirelessnews14-150">[150]</a></sup> Israel-based TinyTap won the education category, Smart Vision Labs of Newport, Rhode Island, won in the healthcare category, and <a href="/wiki/Mosaic_Inc." title="Mosaic Inc.">Mosaic Inc.</a> of Oakland, California, won in the sustainability category.<sup id="cite_ref-Wirelessnews14_150-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wirelessnews14-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Inspire_Her_Mind">Inspire Her Mind</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Inspire Her Mind" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Verizon launched its "Inspire Her Mind" ad in June 2014. The ad, created by the agency AKQA, was designed to encourage girls' interest in science, technology, engineering and math.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> It aimed to address findings from the National Science Foundation, whose research showed that 66 percent of fourth-grade girls said they like science and math, yet only 18 percent of college students in engineering and math are women.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Flipside_Stories_.28.23NeverSettle.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Flipside_Stories_(#NeverSettle)">Flipside Stories (#NeverSettle)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Flipside Stories (#NeverSettle)" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Verizon launched its Flipside Stories ad campaign in February 2015 featuring the #NeverSettle hashtag. The ads show dramatized "testimonials" of people with and without Verizon Wireless or Verizon Fios services.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Better_Matters">Better Matters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Better Matters" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2016, Verizon started using the slogan "Better Matters" in reference to its networks.<sup id="cite_ref-Morrison15_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morrison15-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanability_campaign">Humanability campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Humanability campaign" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Verizon launched its Humanability campaign in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Bruell17_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bruell17-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Slefo17_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slefo17-160">[160]</a></sup> The company aimed for the ads to showcase to consumers and investors its diversification of revenue sources and technology beyond smartphones. These include online advertising, data collection, <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_Things" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet of Things">Internet of Things</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">smart cities</a>, telematics, and media.<sup id="cite_ref-Bruell17_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bruell17-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Slefo17_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slefo17-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_governance">Corporate governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Corporate governance" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_directors">Board of directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Board of directors" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The current board of directors is comprised as follows as of July 2019:<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hans_Vestberg" title="Hans Vestberg">Hans Vestberg</a>, chairman and CEO</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shellye_Archambeau" title="Shellye Archambeau">Shellye Archambeau</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Bertolini" title="Mark Bertolini">Mark Bertolini</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vittorio_Colao" title="Vittorio Colao">Vittorio Colao</a></li>
<li>Melanie Healey, former president of <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clarence_Otis,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Clarence Otis, Jr.">Clarence Otis, Jr.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dan_Schulman" title="Dan Schulman">Daniel H. Schulman</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rodney_E._Slater" title="Rodney E. Slater">Rodney E. Slater</a></li>
<li>Kathryn Tesija, former executive vice president of <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target Corporation</a></li>
<li>Gregory Weaver, former CEO of <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>'s audit and enterprise risk division</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Executives">Executives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Executives" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>As of 2019:<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kapko19_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kapko19-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>Hans Vestberg, chairman and CEO</li>
<li>Ronan Dunne, executive vice president and group CEO, Verizon Consumer</li>
<li>Tami Erwin, executive vice president and group CEO, Verizon Business</li>
<li>Guru Gowrappan, executive vice president and group CEO, Verizon Media</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_responsibility">Corporate responsibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Corporate responsibility" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>The Verizon Foundation is the philanthropic arm of Verizon Communications, donating about $70 million per year to nonprofit organizations, with a focus on education, domestic violence prevention, and energy management.<sup id="cite_ref-Killian08_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Killian08-164">[164]</a></sup> Verizon's educational initiatives have focused on <a href="/wiki/STEM_fields" class="mw-redirect" title="STEM fields">STEM fields</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-JournalofTech12_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JournalofTech12-165">[165]</a></sup> including: a national competition for students to develop mobile application concepts;<sup id="cite_ref-JournalofTech12_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JournalofTech12-165">[165]</a></sup> the Verizon Innovative Learning Schools program, providing professional development for teachers in underserved areas;<sup id="cite_ref-JournalofEng13_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JournalofEng13-166">[166]</a></sup> and providing students with wireless hardware and services as part of President Obama's ConnectED program.<sup id="cite_ref-High14_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-High14-167">[167]</a></sup> The company also runs HopeLine, which has provided mobile phones to approximately 180,000 victims of domestic violence,<sup id="cite_ref-Reznick13_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reznick13-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> and a program that offers grants for victims of domestic violence to start or grow home-based businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-EducationLetter12_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EducationLetter12-170">[170]</a></sup> As part of an initiative to reduce the company's carbon intensity metrics by 50 percent by 2020, Verizon announced planned investment in solar panels and natural gas fuel cells at its facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Fehrenbacher13_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fehrenbacher13-171">[171]</a></sup> The increased capacity would make Verizon the leading solar power producer among U.S. communications companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Mearian14_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mearian14-172">[172]</a></sup></p><p>February 5, 2019, Verizon first entered the green bond market with an issue of $1 billion. The sale was oversubscribed meaning that investors bids wereabout $8 billion. Verizon plans to invest money on renewable energy, for instance, by developing solar and wind energy energy-efficient projects involving technology and equipment replacement, and also the deployment of 5G wireless technologies allowing for real-time response for energy demand (smart building management and city systems), green buildings, sustainable water management, and also biodiversity and conservation.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Cbonds" title="Cbonds">Cbonds</a>, the newly issued green bonds have 3.875% coupon rate and will mature on August 5, 2029. Goldman Sachs and Bank of America Merrill Lynch were the bookrunners of the deal.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Criticism" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_concerns">Security concerns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Security concerns" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>According to Google Project Zero researcher <a href="/wiki/Tavis_Ormandy" title="Tavis Ormandy">Tavis Ormandy</a>, Verizon applies a simplistic certification methodology to give its "Excellence in Information Security Testing" award, e.g. to <a href="/wiki/Comodo_Group" title="Comodo Group">Comodo Group</a>. It focuses on <a href="/wiki/GUI" class="mw-redirect" title="GUI">GUI</a> functions instead of testing security relevant features. Not detected were Chromodo browser disabling of the <a href="/wiki/Same-origin_policy" title="Same-origin policy">same-origin policy</a>, a <a href="/wiki/VNC" class="mw-redirect" title="VNC">VNC</a>-delivered with a default of weak authentication, not enabling address space layout randomization (<a href="/wiki/ASLR" class="mw-redirect" title="ASLR">ASLR</a>) when scanning, and using <a href="/wiki/Access_control_list" class="mw-redirect" title="Access control list">access control lists</a> (ACLs) throughout its product.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Net_neutrality">Net neutrality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Net neutrality" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Verizon and Comcast have been actively lobbying for current changes in the <a href="/wiki/Net_neutrality" title="Net neutrality">FCC's regulations</a> that require internet service providers to offer all content at one internet speed regardless of the type of content since the early 2000s. In 2014, Verizon <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Communications_Inc._v._FCC_(2014)" title="Verizon Communications Inc. v. FCC (2014)">unsuccessfully sued the FCC</a> for these powers.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> Verizon has admitted to throttling content of its competitors including <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> and <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Privacy">Privacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Privacy" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Verizon has a one-star <a href="/wiki/Privacy" title="Privacy">privacy</a> rating from the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Frontier_Foundation" title="Electronic Frontier Foundation">Electronic Frontier Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships_and_venues">Sponsorships and venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sponsorships and venues" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>Verizon is the title sponsor of several large performance and sports venues as well as a sponsor of many major sporting organizations.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Hockey_League">National Hockey League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: National Hockey League" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In January 2007, Verizon secured exclusive marketing and promotional rights with the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DeMarrais07_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeMarrais07-180">[180]</a></sup> The deal was extended for another three years in 2012 and included new provisions for the league to provide exclusive content through Verizon's GameCenter app.<sup id="cite_ref-Long12_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Long12-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsports">Motorsports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Motorsports" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2009 and 2010 Verizon sponsored <a href="/wiki/Justin_Allgaier" title="Justin Allgaier">Justin Allgaier</a> in the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR_Nationwide_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="NASCAR Nationwide Series">NASCAR Nationwide Series</a>, before they chose to opt out of a two-year-old <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> team sponsorship with <a href="/wiki/Team_Penske" title="Team Penske">Penske Racing</a> in order to pursue an expanded presence with the <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Peltz14_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peltz14-182">[182]</a></sup> In March 2014 Verizon signed a multiyear deal making them the title sponsor of the IndyCar Series, now called the Verizon IndyCar Series.<sup id="cite_ref-AP14_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP14-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Football_League">National Football League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: National Football League" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In late 2010, Verizon Communications joined with <a href="/wiki/Vodafone_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Vodafone Group">Vodafone Group</a> in a joint partnership to replace <a href="/wiki/Sprint_Corporation" title="Sprint Corporation">Sprint</a> as the official wireless telecommunications partner of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IEG10_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEG10-184">[184]</a></sup> The four-year deal was estimated at $720 million. In June 2013, Verizon announced a four-year extension with the NFL in a deal reportedly valued at $1 billion. The new agreement gave Verizon the right to stream every NFL regular-season and playoff game.<sup id="cite_ref-sposnorship13_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sposnorship13-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="USA_Team_Handball">USA Team Handball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: USA Team Handball" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In January 2020, Verizon became a founding partner of <a href="/wiki/USA_Team_Handball" title="USA Team Handball">USA Team Handball</a> through the year 2020, with an option to extend the deal until 2024. They are the jersey sponsor for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_handball_team" title="United States national handball team">men's</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_women%27s_national_handball_team" title="United States women's national handball team">women's</a> national handball team and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_national_beach_handball_team" title="United States national beach handball team">men's</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_women%27s_national_beach_handball_team" title="United States women's national beach handball team">women's</a> national beach handball teams. They are presenter of the <a href="/wiki/USA_Team_Handball_College_Nationals" title="USA Team Handball College Nationals">USA Team Handball College Nationals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Venues" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Verizon is the title sponsor for a number of sporting and entertainment arena the <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon Arena">Verizon Arena</a> in North Little Rock, Arkansas;<sup id="cite_ref-VerizonArena_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VerizonArena-187">[187]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Center_(Mankato,_Minnesota)" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon Center (Mankato, Minnesota)">Verizon Center</a> in Mankato, Minnesota.<sup id="cite_ref-FreePress_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FreePress-188">[188]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SNHU_Arena" title="SNHU Arena">SNHU Arena</a> in Manchester, New Hampshire, was originally known as the Verizon Wireless Arena until September 2016, when <a href="/wiki/Southern_New_Hampshire_University" title="Southern New Hampshire University">Southern New Hampshire University</a> acquired the naming rights for a period of at least 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-SNHU_Partners_with_SMG_Group_for_Arena_Naming_Rights_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SNHU_Partners_with_SMG_Group_for_Arena_Naming_Rights-189">[189]</a></sup></p><p>Verizon has been the title sponsor of entertainment amphitheaters in locations throughout the United States, including four individually referred to as the "Verizon Wireless Amphitheatre": in Irvine, California;<sup id="cite_ref-Morrison16_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morrison16-190">[190]</a></sup> Maryland Heights, Missouri;<sup id="cite_ref-Feldt14_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldt14-191">[191]</a></sup> Selma, Texas;<sup id="cite_ref-Levy11_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levy11-192">[192]</a></sup> and Alpharetta, Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-Hensley18_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hensley18-193">[193]</a></sup></p><p>Verizon was the former sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/Capital_One_Arena" title="Capital One Arena">Capital One Arena</a> in Washington, DC;<sup id="cite_ref-Nakamura07_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nakamura07-194">[194]</a></sup></p><p>The main home concert hall of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Orchestra" title="Philadelphia Orchestra">Philadelphia Orchestra</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Kimmel_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Kimmel Center for the Performing Arts">Kimmel Center for the Performing Arts</a> is named Verizon Hall.<sup id="cite_ref-Oestreich01_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oestreich01-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Verizon_Communications&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
